The Three Types of Qidam and Huduth
Defines the three types of qidam and huduth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of qidam and huduth — essential, temporal, and relative — and how they relate to each other in scope.

Core Idea
Essential qidam is the strictest; relative huduth is the broadest.

The theological terms 'qadim' and 'hadith' are not simple. They can mean different things depending on what kind of 'precedence' is being considered. In this passage, the author lays out the three distinct senses and shows how they interrelate.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice how each type is defined by what it is not preceded by.
Essential: not preceded by any other. Temporal: not preceded by non-existence. Relative: longer past time.
2
Compare the scopes
Identify which type is most specific and which is broadest. The passage explains the logical relationships.
Essential qidam is most specific; relative huduth is most specific (i.e., most things are relatively recent).
3
Apply the concepts
Think of examples: God is essential qadim. The heavens might be temporal qadim for philosophers. A father is relatively older than his son.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الأول في تفسيرهما وأقسامهما وما يتعلق بذلك (المبحث الأول : (۱) قد يراد بهما(۲) عدم المسبوقيـة بـالـغيـر والمسبوقية (۳) بــه (٤) ، وقد يخص الغير بالعدم وهو المتعارف، وقد يقالان باعتبار تفاوت ما مضى من زمان الوجود زيادة ونقصا، فالقدم الذاتي أخص من الزماني، وهو من الإضافي والحدوث بالعكس . والمتصف بهما حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، وقد يتصف بهما العدم، فيقال للعدم الغير المسبوق بالوجود قديم، وللمسبوق حادث، ثم كل من القدم والحدوث قد يوجد حقيقياً، وقد يوجد (ه) إضافياً. أما الحقيقي فقد يراد بالقدم عدم المسبوقية بالغير، وبالحدوث المسبوقية به، ويسمى ذاتياً، وقد يخص الغير بالعدم، فيراد بالقدم عدم المسبوقية بالعدم، وبالحدوث المسبوقية به، وهو معنى الخروج من العدم إلى الوجود، زمانياً، وهذا (٦) هو المتعارف عند الجمهور، وأما الإضافي، فيراد بالقدم كون ما مضى من زمان وجود الشيء أكثر، وبالحدوث كونه أقل. ويسمى فالقدم الذاتي أخص من الزماني والزماني من الإضافي، بمعنى أن كل ما ليس مسبوقا بالغير أصلاً ليس مسبوقاً بالعدم ولا عكس، كما في صفات الواجب وكل ما ليس مسبوقاً بالعدم، فما مضى من زمان وجوده يكون أكثر بالنسبة إلى ما حدث بعده ولا عكس كالأب فإنه أقدم من الابن، وليس قديماً بالزمان، والحدوث الإضافي أخص من الزماني، والزماني من الذاتي، بمعنى أن كل ما يكون زمان وجوده الماضي أقل فهو (۱) مسبوق بالعدم، ولا عكس، وكل ما هو مسبوق بالعدم، فهو مسبوق بالغير ولا عكس . قال : لا قديم بالذات (۲) سوى الله تعالى (۳) ، وأمـا بـالـزمـان (٤) فزادت الفلاسفة كثيراً من الممكنات (٥) ، والمتكلمون صفات الله تعالى (٦)، ولزم المعتزلة حيث جعلوا العالمية ،والقادرية والحيية والموجدية، أحوالاً ثابتة في الأزل مع الذات، ولا نعني بالوجود إلا ما عنوا بالثبوت) . ، لما سيأتي من أدلة توحيد الواجب، وما وقع في عبارة بعضهم، من (۷) أن صفات الله تعالى واجبة أو قديمة بالذات فمعناه بذات الواجب بمعنى أنها لا تفتقر إلى غير الذات. وأما القديم بالزمان فجعله الفلاسفة شاملاً لكثير من الممكنات كالمجردات والأفلاك وغير ذلك على ما سيأتي . والمتكلمون منا لصفات الله تعالى فقط، حيث بينوا أن ما سوى ذات
The first investigation: concerning the interpretation of the two (qidam and huduth) and their divisions and what pertains to that. (First investigation:) (1) Sometimes by them are intended the absence of being preceded by another and being preceded by another (2)(3)(4), and sometimes 'another' is specified as non-existence, and that is the conventional meaning. And they are sometimes said with consideration of the difference of what has passed of the time of existence, increase and decrease. So essential qidam (qidam dhati) is more specific than temporal qidam, and it is more specific than relative qidam, and huduth is the opposite. That which is truly described by them is existence, while the existent is so by consideration of it. And sometimes non-existence is described by them, so non-existence not preceded by existence is called qadim, and preceded is called hadith. Then each of qidam and huduth may be found as real (haqiqi) and may be found as relative (idafi). As for the real: sometimes by qidam is meant the absence of being preceded by another, and by huduth being preceded by it, and it is called essential (dhati). And sometimes 'another' is specified as non-existence, so by qidam is meant the absence of being preceded by non-existence, and by huduth being preceded by it, and that is the meaning of emergence from non-existence into existence, temporal. And this is the conventional meaning among the majority. As for the relative: by qidam is meant that what has passed of the time of existence of a thing is more, and by huduth that it is less. And it is called. So essential qidam is more specific than temporal, and temporal than relative, meaning that everything not preceded by another at all is not preceded by non-existence, and not vice versa, as in the attributes of the Necessary Being. And everything not preceded by non-existence, then what has passed of its time of existence is more relative to what occurred after it, and not vice versa, like the father, for he is older than the son, but not qadim by time. And relative huduth is more specific than temporal, and temporal than essential, meaning that everything of which the past time of existence is less is preceded by non-existence, and not vice versa; and everything preceded by non-existence is preceded by another, and not vice versa. He said: There is no qadim by essence (2) except Allah the Exalted (3). As for by time (4), the philosophers added many possibles (5), and the theologians (added) the attributes of Allah the Exalted (6). And it followed for the Mu'tazila, since they made 'being knowing', 'being powerful', 'being living', and 'being causing' as states (ahwal) subsisting in pre-eternity with the essence, and we do not mean by existence except what they meant by subsistence. Due to what will come of the proofs of the unity of the Necessary Being, and what occurred in the expression of some of them, that the attributes of Allah the Exalted are necessary or qadim by essence, so its meaning is by the essence of the Necessary Being, in the sense that they do not need anything other than the essence. As for the qadim by time, the philosophers made it inclusive of many possibles, such as the immaterial substances, the spheres, and other things, as will come. And the theologians from us (apply it) to the attributes of Allah the Exalted only, as they showed that what is other than the essence...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies the terms qidam (eternity/past eternity) and huduth (origination/temporal beginning) in multiple senses. It begins by stating the general meanings: 'not preceded by another' (qidam) and 'preceded by another' (huduth), where 'another' is conventionally understood as non-existence. It then distinguishes three types: essential (dhati), temporal (zamani), and relative (idafi). Essential qidam is the absence of being preceded by any other; temporal qidam is the absence of being preceded by non-existence (i.e., having always existed in time); relative qidam is having a longer past duration. The text explains that existence is the true subject of these attributes, but non-existence can also be described as qadim or hadith in a relative sense. It then compares the scopes: essential qidam is most specific (only God), temporal qidam includes more (God's attributes according to theologians, or certain possibles according to philosophers), and relative qidam is even broader (e.g., a father is relatively older than his son). The passage then cites the principle 'There is no qadim by essence except Allah', and explains that philosophers consider many possible beings as qadim by time, while theologians reserve temporal qidam for God's attributes. It notes that the Mu'tazila, who posit divine attributes as states (ahwal) subsisting in pre-eternity with the essence, essentially equate existence with subsistence, leading to a consequence. Finally, it clarifies that when some say attributes are 'qadim by essence', it means they are necessary by God's essence, not independent. The passage concludes by noting that philosophers extend temporal qidam to immaterial substances and spheres, while theologians restrict it to God's attributes.

Key Terms
قدم
حدوث
قدم ذاتي
قدم زماني
قدم إضافي
عدم المسبوقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that temporal qidam is the same as essential qidam.
Correction: Essential qidam means not preceded by any other, which is unique to God. Temporal qidam means not preceded by non-existence, which can apply to created things that have always existed in time, like God's attributes according to some.

Checkpoint
Which type of qidam is defined as 'not preceded by any other (other than non-existence)'?
A) Essential qidam
B) Temporal qidam
C) Relative qidam
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The terms qidam and huduth have three distinct meanings: essential, temporal, and relative, with essential being the most specific sense of qidam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the concept of essential qidam (not being preceded by any other), does your understanding of God's absolute priority change how you view your own existence as something that is originated? How does this affect your reliance on Him?
?
The passage distinguishes between temporal huduth (being preceded by non-existence) and relative huduth (being shorter in duration). Consider your own life: in what ways do you experience both types of huduth? How does this knowledge make you more aware of your dependence on the Eternal?
?
If relative huduth is the most specific sense of huduth, meaning that everything created is in some way 'newer' relative to something else, what does that say about your own status before God? Are you humbled by the fact that even your existence is a recent event in the grand scheme? How should this affect your daily gratitude?

Who or What is Qadim? God, Attributes, and Philosophers
Explains the scope of qidam and differences among schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the application of the different types of qidam to different beings, and the differences between theologians, philosophers, and the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Only God is essential qadim; others may be temporal or relative qadim.

Having defined the types of qidam, the passage now applies them to real entities. It states the principle 'لا قديم بالذات سوى الله' and then explains how philosophers and theologians differ on temporal qadim.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle
Read the statement 'There is no qadim by essence except Allah'. This is a key theological claim.
2
Identify different views
Note that philosophers attribute temporal qidam to possibles like immaterial substances and spheres, while theologians attribute it only to God's attributes.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila issue
The passage mentions the Mu'tazila's view of attributes as states (ahwal) and how they equate existence with subsistence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الأول في تفسيرهما وأقسامهما وما يتعلق بذلك (المبحث الأول : (۱) قد يراد بهما(۲) عدم المسبوقيـة بـالـغيـر والمسبوقية (۳) بــه (٤) ، وقد يخص الغير بالعدم وهو المتعارف، وقد يقالان باعتبار تفاوت ما مضى من زمان الوجود زيادة ونقصا، فالقدم الذاتي أخص من الزماني، وهو من الإضافي والحدوث بالعكس . والمتصف بهما حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، وقد يتصف بهما العدم، فيقال للعدم الغير المسبوق بالوجود قديم، وللمسبوق حادث، ثم كل من القدم والحدوث قد يوجد حقيقياً، وقد يوجد (ه) إضافياً. أما الحقيقي فقد يراد بالقدم عدم المسبوقية بالغير، وبالحدوث المسبوقية به، ويسمى ذاتياً، وقد يخص الغير بالعدم، فيراد بالقدم عدم المسبوقية بالعدم، وبالحدوث المسبوقية به، وهو معنى الخروج من العدم إلى الوجود، زمانياً، وهذا (٦) هو المتعارف عند الجمهور، وأما الإضافي، فيراد بالقدم كون ما مضى من زمان وجود الشيء أكثر، وبالحدوث كونه أقل. ويسمى فالقدم الذاتي أخص من الزماني والزماني من الإضافي، بمعنى أن كل ما ليس مسبوقا بالغير أصلاً ليس مسبوقاً بالعدم ولا عكس، كما في صفات الواجب وكل ما ليس مسبوقاً بالعدم، فما مضى من زمان وجوده يكون أكثر بالنسبة إلى ما حدث بعده ولا عكس كالأب فإنه أقدم من الابن، وليس قديماً بالزمان، والحدوث الإضافي أخص من الزماني، والزماني من الذاتي، بمعنى أن كل ما يكون زمان وجوده الماضي أقل فهو (۱) مسبوق بالعدم، ولا عكس، وكل ما هو مسبوق بالعدم، فهو مسبوق بالغير ولا عكس . قال : لا قديم بالذات (۲) سوى الله تعالى (۳) ، وأمـا بـالـزمـان (٤) فزادت الفلاسفة كثيراً من الممكنات (٥) ، والمتكلمون صفات الله تعالى (٦)، ولزم المعتزلة حيث جعلوا العالمية ،والقادرية والحيية والموجدية، أحوالاً ثابتة في الأزل مع الذات، ولا نعني بالوجود إلا ما عنوا بالثبوت) . ، لما سيأتي من أدلة توحيد الواجب، وما وقع في عبارة بعضهم، من (۷) أن صفات الله تعالى واجبة أو قديمة بالذات فمعناه بذات الواجب بمعنى أنها لا تفتقر إلى غير الذات. وأما القديم بالزمان فجعله الفلاسفة شاملاً لكثير من الممكنات كالمجردات والأفلاك وغير ذلك على ما سيأتي . والمتكلمون منا لصفات الله تعالى فقط، حيث بينوا أن ما سوى ذات
The first investigation: concerning the interpretation of the two (qidam and huduth) and their divisions and what pertains to that. (First investigation:) (1) Sometimes by them are intended the absence of being preceded by another and being preceded by another (2)(3)(4), and sometimes 'another' is specified as non-existence, and that is the conventional meaning. And they are sometimes said with consideration of the difference of what has passed of the time of existence, increase and decrease. So essential qidam (qidam dhati) is more specific than temporal qidam, and it is more specific than relative qidam, and huduth is the opposite. That which is truly described by them is existence, while the existent is so by consideration of it. And sometimes non-existence is described by them, so non-existence not preceded by existence is called qadim, and preceded is called hadith. Then each of qidam and huduth may be found as real (haqiqi) and may be found as relative (idafi). As for the real: sometimes by qidam is meant the absence of being preceded by another, and by huduth being preceded by it, and it is called essential (dhati). And sometimes 'another' is specified as non-existence, so by qidam is meant the absence of being preceded by non-existence, and by huduth being preceded by it, and that is the meaning of emergence from non-existence into existence, temporal. And this is the conventional meaning among the majority. As for the relative: by qidam is meant that what has passed of the time of existence of a thing is more, and by huduth that it is less. And it is called. So essential qidam is more specific than temporal, and temporal than relative, meaning that everything not preceded by another at all is not preceded by non-existence, and not vice versa, as in the attributes of the Necessary Being. And everything not preceded by non-existence, then what has passed of its time of existence is more relative to what occurred after it, and not vice versa, like the father, for he is older than the son, but not qadim by time. And relative huduth is more specific than temporal, and temporal than essential, meaning that everything of which the past time of existence is less is preceded by non-existence, and not vice versa; and everything preceded by non-existence is preceded by another, and not vice versa. He said: There is no qadim by essence (2) except Allah the Exalted (3). As for by time (4), the philosophers added many possibles (5), and the theologians (added) the attributes of Allah the Exalted (6). And it followed for the Mu'tazila, since they made 'being knowing', 'being powerful', 'being living', and 'being causing' as states (ahwal) subsisting in pre-eternity with the essence, and we do not mean by existence except what they meant by subsistence. Due to what will come of the proofs of the unity of the Necessary Being, and what occurred in the expression of some of them, that the attributes of Allah the Exalted are necessary or qadim by essence, so its meaning is by the essence of the Necessary Being, in the sense that they do not need anything other than the essence. And the theologians from us (apply it) to the attributes of Allah the Exalted only, as they showed that what is other than the essence...

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies the terms qidam (eternity/past eternity) and huduth (origination/temporal beginning) in multiple senses. It begins by stating the general meanings: 'not preceded by another' (qidam) and 'preceded by another' (huduth), where 'another' is conventionally understood as non-existence. It then distinguishes three types: essential (dhati), temporal (zamani), and relative (idafi). Essential qidam is the absence of being preceded by any other; temporal qidam is the absence of being preceded by non-existence (i.e., having always existed in time); relative qidam is having a longer past duration. The text explains that existence is the true subject of these attributes, but non-existence can also be described as qadim or hadith in a relative sense. It then compares the scopes: essential qidam is most specific (only God), temporal qidam includes more (God's attributes according to theologians, or certain possibles according to philosophers), and relative qidam is even broader (e.g., a father is relatively older than his son). The passage then cites the principle 'There is no qadim by essence except Allah', and explains that philosophers consider many possible beings as qadim by time, while theologians reserve temporal qidam for God's attributes. It notes that the Mu'tazila, who posit divine attributes as states (ahwal) subsisting in pre-eternity with the essence, essentially equate existence with subsistence, leading to a consequence. Finally, it clarifies that when some say attributes are 'qadim by essence', it means they are necessary by God's essence, not independent. The passage concludes by noting that philosophers extend temporal qidam to immaterial substances and spheres, while theologians restrict it to God's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly recognize in your heart that nothing in this universe—no person, no idea, no possession—is eternal except Allah? What competes with this exclusivity in your daily life?
?
Have you ever treated something created as though it were uncreated, giving it a permanence that only Allah deserves? How will you realign your heart today?
?
If God alone is essential qadim, what does that mean for your own fleeting existence? How does this truth shape your priorities and the way you spend your limited time?

Definition of Ijab and Its Implication
Defines ijab and resolves an objection about essential necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of ijab (necessitation) in Kalam and why it does not entail essential necessity.

Core Idea
Necessitation does not make something essentially necessary; necessity comes from the cause, not the essence.

This lesson introduces a key causal concept in Kalam: ijab, or necessitation. The author defines it and then addresses a natural objection: if something is necessitated, doesn't that make it necessary? The distinction he draws is crucial for understanding the relationship between God and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the two parts: the definition and the objection-answer exchange.
The passage is short but dense. Read slowly.
2
Identify the definition and objection
Identify what 'ijab' is defined as and what the objection claims. The objection says the effect would then be necessary.
Look for the phrase 'فإن قيل' which introduces the objection.
3
Understand the answer
The author answers by distinguishing between impossibility of non-existence due to a complete cause and essential necessity. Grasp this distinction.
This distinction prevents conflating created things with the Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيجاب ابتداء أو انتهاء، لامتناع التسلسل من غير توقف على شرط حادث ضرورة، فلو عدم عدم الواجب. فإن قيل: فلا يكون إلا واجباً. قلنا: امتناع العدم لتمام علة الوجود لا يستلزم الوجوب الذاتي.
Necessitation (al-ījāb) is at the beginning or end, due to the impossibility of infinite regress without depending on a temporal condition necessarily, for if it were non-existent, the Necessary would be non-existent. If it is said: Then it is only necessary (wājib). We say: The impossibility of non-existence due to the completeness of the cause of existence does not entail essential necessity (al-wujūb al-dhātī).
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of ījāb (necessitation or efficient causation with necessity) and clarifies that it does not imply essential necessity (wujūb dhātī). The author states that ījāb occurs at the beginning or end of a causal chain, because an infinite regress without a temporal condition is impossible. If the necessitation were absent, then the Necessary Being would also be absent (which is impossible). An objection is raised: if the effect is necessitated, then it must be necessary (wājib). The author answers: the impossibility of its non-existence is due to the completeness of its cause, not to its own essence. Therefore, it does not become necessary in itself (wājib bi-dhātihī), but only conditionally necessary. This distinction is crucial in Kalām to avoid pantheism or determinism.

Key Terms
الإيجاب
الوجوب الذاتي
امتناع العدم
تمام العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any necessitated being is essentially necessary.
Correction: An effect's impossibility of non-existence may be due to its complete cause, not its own essence, so it is only conditionally necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that a necessitated effect is not essentially necessary?
A) Because it is eternal
B) Because its impossibility of non-existence is due to the completeness of its cause, not its own essence
C) Because it depends on a temporal condition
D) Because it is impossible for it to be essential

Key Takeaway
Ijab does not imply essential necessity; the impossibility of non-existence due to a complete cause is not the same as being necessary in itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there beliefs or habits in your life that you treat as 'essentially necessary'—things you think you cannot change—when in reality they are only conditionally necessary due to external causes? What one such false necessity will you challenge this week, and what first step can you take to break it?
?
The objector assumes that if something is necessitated, it is necessary in itself. Have you ever held a similar assumption about your own limitations, thinking 'I am just this way' without recognizing that your situation is caused and therefore changeable? What would it take to truly internalize that your current state is not your essence?
?
This lesson shows that the impossibility of non-existence due to a cause is not the same as being inherently necessary. In your spiritual life, do you sometimes confuse external compulsions (e.g., peer pressure, cultural norms) with genuine divine obligations? How can you use this distinction to purify your intentions?

Necessity of a Simple Eternal Matter for Composites
Argues that composites require a simple eternal matter to avoid infinite regress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why composite beings require a simple, eternal matter to avoid an infinite regress of substrates.

Core Idea
Every composite needs a simple, eternal foundation to stop an infinite chain.

This lesson presents a key argument from kalam cosmology: every composite thing must have a simple, eternal substrate. The author argues that if the substrate itself were originated, it would lead to an infinite regress, which is impossible. Let's examine this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the gist.
The beginning 'تركب عنها' may refer to a preceding argument about composition.
2
Identify the key terms
Find and understand the terms: مادة (matter), مركب (composite), حادث (originated), قديم (eternal), تسلسل (infinite regress).
These terms are central to the argument.
3
Understand the argument against infinite regress
Notice that if the matter of a composite were originated (haditha), it would itself require another matter, leading to an infinite chain (tasalsul). This is deemed impossible.
The argument uses reduction to absurdity.
4
Contrast with motion and time
The passage notes that motion and time are finite and determinate, so they do not need such an eternal substrate.
This clarifies the scope of the argument.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that there must exist a simple eternal matter that serves as the substrate for originated forms and accidents.
This matter is not necessarily uncreated; it only avoids regress in this specific chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تركب عنها وهو محال لما سيأتي بخلاف الحركة والزمان، فإنهما على التحديد والانقضاء ، بل بمعنى أنه لا بد أن يكون للمركب مادة بسيطة قديمة، هي الحاصل للصور والأعراض الحادثة ، إذ لو كانت حادثة لكانت لها مادة أخرى وتسلسل .
Composed of them, and it is impossible because of what will come, unlike motion and time, for they are upon determination and termination. Rather, it means that the composite must have a simple eternal matter, which is the substrate for originated forms and accidents. For if it were originated, it would require another matter and [lead to] infinite regress.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of a simple eternal matter (madda) underlying composed bodies. The author argues that any composite must have a matter (madda) that is simple (basita) and eternal (qadima); if the matter itself were originated (haditha), it would itself require a matter, and so on ad infinitum (tasalsul). This infinite regress is impossible, so there must be a matter that is not originated. The passage contrasts this with motion and time, which are 'determined and finite' (ala al-tahdid wa al-inqida'), implying they do not require such a substrate.

Correction: The passage only argues that matter must not be originated in this specific chain to avoid infinite regress; it does not assert that matter is uncreated in an absolute sense.

?
An infinite regress of excuses is impossible—there must be a stopping point. What patterns of behavior or thought do you keep 'deferring' with temporary fixes, avoiding the real, simple change? What would it mean to face that foundational issue today?

The passage contrasts composites (which need a substrate) with motion and time (which are determined and finite). What one thing can you strip away to simplify your devotion?

Proof for Matter from Possibility
Proof for matter from possibility of the originated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam argument that the possibility of an originated thing requires a subject (matter) distinct from both the thing itself and the agent.

Core Idea
Possibility is a real accident that must inhere in matter.

Theologians (mutakallimun) argue that before an originated thing exists, it is 'possible'—neither necessary nor impossible. This possibility, they claim, is not just a mental concept but a real property that requires a substrate. The following passage presents this proof step by step, showing that the substrate cannot be the thing itself (which doesn't exist yet) nor the agent (since possibility grounds power, not vice versa), concluding that it must be a pre-existing matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the flow of the argument from the possibility of the originated to the existence of matter.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main premise and conclusion
The first sentence states the conclusion: 'They argued for the existence of matter...'. Trace how each subsequent statement supports this.
The proof uses several negative and positive steps.
3
Understand the nature of possibility (imkan)
The passage asserts that possibility is an existent accident (wujudi) and not a substance, because it is relational (idafi). This is crucial to the proof.
Recall that substances are self-subsistent; accidents require a subject.
4
Examine the refutation of the alternative view
The passage rejects the idea that possibility is the agent's power. Note the reasoning: power depends on possibility, not the other way around.
This shows the independence of possibility from the agent.
5
Formulate the complete argument in your own words
Try to reconstruct the proof from start to finish, explaining why matter is necessary.
This will solidify your understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجوا على ثبوت المادة بأن الحادث قبل وجوده ممكن لامتناع الانقلاب وكل ممكن فله إمكان ، وهو وجودي لما سبق من الأدلة، وليس بجوهر لكونه إضافياً بحقيقته، فيكون عرضاً، فيستدعي محلاً موجوداً ليس هو نفس ذلك الحادث، لامتناع تقدم الشيء على نفسه، ولا أمراً منفصلاً عنه، لأنه لا معنى لقيام إمكان الشيء بالأمر المنفصل عنه بل متعلقاً به، وهو المعنى بالمادة، وما توهم من أن إمكان الشيء هو اقتدار الفاعل عليه فيكون قائماً بالفاعل فاسداً، لأنه معلل بالإمكان وعدمه بعدمه، فيقال. هذا مقدور لكونه ممكناً، وذاك غير مقدور لكونه ممتنعاً ، ولأنه لا يكون إلا بالقياس إلى القادر بخلاف الإمكان .
They argued for the existence of matter by [saying] that the originated thing before its existence is possible because of the impossibility of change [from impossible to possible], and every possible has possibility, and it is existent [as an accident] based on previous proofs, and it is not a substance because it is relational in its reality, so it is an accident. Thus it requires an existing subject that is not that same originated thing, because a thing cannot precede itself, and not something separate from it, because there is no meaning to the subsistence of a thing's possibility in a separate thing, but [it subsists] in something related to it, and that is the meaning of matter. And what is imagined that the possibility of a thing is the power of the agent over it, so it subsists in the agent, is corrupt, because [power] is caused by possibility and its absence by its absence; thus it is said: this is possible because it is possible, and that is not possible because it is impossible, and because [power] is only relative to the powerful contrary to possibility.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage presents the kalam proof for the existence of matter (madda) from the concept of possibility (imkan). The argument runs: (1) An originated thing (hadith) before its existence is possible (mumkin) because change from impossibility to possibility is impossible. (2) Every possible has a property of possibility (imkan), which is an existent accident (wujudi) as proven earlier. (3) This possibility cannot be a substance because it is relational (idafi); hence it is an accident (arad). (4) As an accident, it requires a subject (mahall) that is (a) not the originated thing itself (since it precedes it), and (b) not separate from it (since possibility relates to the thing). (5) That subject is matter. The passage then refutes a misconception: some imagine possibility is the agent's power, but power depends on possibility, not vice versa.

Key Terms
إمكان
حادث
عرض
مادة
جوهر
إضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility is the same as the agent's power to create.
Correction: The passage shows that power depends on possibility (something is possible first, then power applies), and possibility is independent of the agent.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why can possibility not inhere in the originated thing itself?
A) Because the originated thing does not yet exist
B) Because possibility is a substance
C) Because the agent's power is the subject
D) Because matter already exists

Key Takeaway
The possibility of an originated thing is a real accident that must inhere in a pre-existing subject, which is matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that the possibility of your existence inhered in matter before you were born. How does that reshape your understanding of your reliance on the created world, and what steps can you take today to live in humble awareness of that dependence?
?
Your ability to choose and act is dependent on the possibility of your actions—not the other way around. Are you living as if your power creates possibilities, or are you submitting your plans to the reality that possibility precedes your power? What would change if you truly admitted that?
?
If the agent's power is caused by possibility, then even your most determined efforts are contingent on what is possible. Does that thought disturb you or liberate you? How will you remind yourself of this limit in your daily decisions?

Objection from Eternal Possible Things and Reply
Presents and answers the objection that eternal possible things have no matter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument from possibility is defended against the objection of eternal possible things that lack matter.

Core Idea
Eternal possible things have no 'before' — their possibility does not need a subject.

This passage presents a classic objection to the kalam cosmological argument: if possibility requires a subject (matter), what about eternal possible things like separate intellects that have no matter? The reply is subtle but decisive — eternal things have no state before existence, so their possibility is intrinsic, not a property needing an external bearer. Let's see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic and translation of the objection carefully. Note that the objector claims eternal possible things (mumkin qadim) like matters and separate substances have no matter, yet they are possible, so the proof fails.
The objection targets the proof that possibility requires a material substrate.
2
Study the reply
Read the reply: the possibilities of these eternal things are qa'im biha — subsistent in themselves. Because they have no 'state before existence', their possibility does not require another subject.
The key phrase is 'إمكاناتها قائمة بها'.
3
Connect to the doctrine of eternal things
Reflect on what 'eternal' means in kalam: things that have always existed, like the intellects. They have no temporal beginning, so their possibility is not a property that comes to them; it is inseparable from their essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الدليل منقوض بالممكن القديم كالمواد والمجردات، فإنها ممكنة، ولا مادة لها . قلنا : إمكاناتها قائمة بها إذ ليس للقديم حالة ما قبل الوجود، حتى يكون هناك إمكان يستدعي محلا غيره .
If it is said: The proof is invalidated by the eternal possible things like the matters and the separate substances, for they are possible and have no matter. We say: Their possibilities are subsistent in them, since the eternal has no state before existence such that there would be a possibility requiring another subject.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer unit. The objector notes that the proof from possibility would also apply to eternal possible things (al-mumkin al-qadim) such as the prime matters (mawadd) and separate intellects (mujarradat). These are possible in themselves but have no matter, so the argument fails. The answer: eternal things have no 'state before existence' (hala ma qabl al-wujud) in which their possibility would need a subject other than themselves. Their possibility is inherent (qa'imatu biha) in their essences, not requiring an external subject like matter.

Key Terms

مجردات
مواد
إمكان
مادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The reply denies that eternal things are possible.
Correction: The reply does not deny their possibility; it merely argues that their possibility does not demand a subject because they have no state before existence.

Checkpoint

A) It denies that eternal things are possible
B) It asserts that their possibility subsists in themselves, not requiring another subject
C) It claims eternal things do have matter
D) It argues that the proof only applies to originated things

Key Takeaway
Eternal possible things have an intrinsic possibility that does not require an external subject because they have no state before existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How would learning to distinguish between temporal and eternal possibility help you in your journey to truth? Will you commit to examining objections to important beliefs more carefully?

Separating Two Kinds of Possibility: Essential vs. Preparatory
Answers the objection by distinguishing essential from preparatory possibility and listing three differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why essential possibility is merely a mental consideration while preparatory possibility is a real quality that inheres in matter, and how this distinction resolves the objection that possibility requires an existing subject.

Core Idea
Possibility is not one thing; essential possibility is mental, preparatory possibility is real and in matter.

The second objection claims that possibility, being a quality, must inhere in an existing subject—but then the discussion of possibility before existence would be nonsense. The answer cuts through this by showing that the objector conflates two entirely different kinds of possibility. By distinguishing essential possibility (a logical category) from preparatory possibility (a real property of matter), the author defends the proof for matter and the necessity of a pre-existing subject. Let's follow the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the objection (starting 'فإن قيل') and the answer ('قلنا' then 'والجواب').
This is a dense paragraph; reading it through once will help you see the structure.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The answer distinguishes 'essential possibility' (الإمكان الذاتي) from 'preparatory possibility' (الإمكان الاستعدادي). Locate where each is defined and note the key phrase that essential possibility is a mental consideration (اعتبار عقلي).
The objector assumed all possibility is the same type.
3
Study the three differences
The passage lists three differences between the two types. Read each one carefully and understand how they contrast. The differences are enumerated with 'أحدها', 'ثانيها', 'ثالثها'.
These differences form the core of the distinction.
4
Reflect on the objection's resolution
Ask yourself: How does this distinction answer the objection? The objector said possibility needs an existing subject. Essential possibility does not (it's mental). Preparatory possibility does, but only in matter (which exists). So the objection fails.
This links back to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إمكان الشيء صفة له، فلا يقوم إلا به ، ولو سلم قيامه بمحله كما في الصور والأعراض، لم يكن ذلك إلا حال وجودهما، والكلام فيما قبل الوجود . قلنا سنورد من كلامهم ما يدفع هذا الإشكال والجواب : أنه إن أريد بالإمكان الإمكان الذاتي اللازم لماهية الممكن، فلا نسلم أنه وجودي، بمعنى كونه أمراً محققاً يستدعي محلاً موجوداً في الخارج، وقد مر بيان ضعف أدلتهم على ذلك، وإن أريد الإمكان الاستعدادي، فلا نسلم أن كل حادث فهو قبل وجوده ممكن بالإمكان الاستعدادي لجواز أن يحدث من غير أن يكون هناك مادة وأمور معدة لها ، إلى وجود ذلك الحادث، ولا يكون هذا من الانقلاب في شيء، لأن المقابل للوجوب والامتناع هو الإمكان الذاتي، لا الاستعدادي، وفي قوله المخالف له إشارة إلى التغاير بين الإمكانين، وذلك من وجوه . أحدها : أن الذاتي لا يقتضي رجحان الوجود أو العدم، بل كلاهما بالنظر إليه على السواء، والاستعدادي يقتضيه لأنه حالة مقربة للمادة إلى تأثير المؤثر فيها وإيجاد الحادث . وثانيها : أن الاستعدادي يتفاوت بالقرب والبعد فإن استعداد المضغة للإنسانية، أقرب من استعداد العلقة ، وهو من المادة النباتية ، وهو من المعدنية، وهو من العنصرية وهكذا حتى أن الهيولى الأولى أبعد الكل ولا كذلك الإمكان الذاتي. فإنه لا يتصور تفاوت واختلاف في إمكان وجود الإنسان لماهيته، وما توهم من تفاوته عند اعتبار التعلق بأمر خارج، كإمكان وجود الإنسان لماهيته بالنظر إلى العلقة والمضغة مثلاً، فعائد إلى الاستعدادي . وثالثهما أن الذاتي اعتبار عقلى ولا تحقق له في الأعيان بخلاف الاستعدادي، فإنه كيفية حاصلة للشيء، مهيئة إياه لإفاضة الفاعل وجود
If it is said: The possibility of a thing is a quality of it, so it subsists only in it; and even if it is granted that it subsists in its subject as in forms and accidents, that would only be in the state of their existence, but the discussion is about before existence. We said: We will bring from their speech what repels this difficulty. And the answer: If by 'possibility' is meant essential possibility which is necessary for the essence of the possible, then we do not accept that it is existent in the sense of being a real thing requiring an existing subject in the external world, and the weakness of their proofs for that has been mentioned. And if by 'possibility' is meant preparatory possibility, then we do not accept that every originated thing before its existence is possible with preparatory possibility, because it is possible that it occurs without there being a matter and preparatory things [leading] to the existence of that originated thing, and this is not a [case of] change at all, because the opposite of necessity and impossibility is essential possibility, not preparatory possibility. In the statement of the opponent there is an indication of the difference between the two possibilities, and that is in several respects. One: essential possibility does not imply preference for existence or non-existence; both are equal with respect to it, while preparatory possibility implies preference because it is a state that brings the matter closer to the influence of the agent and the generation of the originated thing. Second: preparatory possibility varies in proximity and distance, for the preparation of the morsel for humanity is closer than the preparation of the clot, and that of the plant matter is [closer], and that of the mineral, and that of the element, and so on until the primary matter is the farthest of all. Essential possibility does not admit variation and difference in the possibility of the existence of a human for its essence, and what is imagined of its variation when considering relation to an external thing, like the possibility of human existence for its essence in relation to the clot and morsel for example, returns to preparatory possibility. Third: essential possibility is a mental consideration and has no realization in external things, unlike preparatory possibility, for it is a quality acquired by the thing, preparing it for the agent to bestow existence.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the answer to the second objection. The objector argues that possibility is a quality (sifa) of the thing itself, so it cannot inhere in another subject; even if it could, that would only be during existence, not before. The answer distinguishes two types of possibility: essential (al-imkan al-dhati) and preparatory (al-imkan al-isti'dadi). Essential possibility is a mental consideration (i'tibar 'aqli) with no extramental reality, so it does not require a subject in the outside. Preparatory possibility is a real quality (kayfiyya hasila) that inheres in a subject (matter) and prepares it for receiving existence. The author then gives three differences: (1) essential possibility is indifferent to existence/non-existence, while preparatory gives preference; (2) preparatory varies in degree, essential does not; (3) essential is mental, preparatory is real. The passage clarifies that the opponents' argument mistakenly treats all possibility as essential, but the proof for matter relies on preparatory possibility.

Key Terms
إمكان ذاتي
إمكان استعدادي
مادة
هيولى
اعتبار عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All possibility is a real quality requiring an existing subject.
Correction: Essential possibility is merely a mental consideration (i'tibar 'aqli) with no external reality, so it does not require a subject. Only preparatory possibility is real and inheres in matter.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what is the fundamental difference between essential possibility and preparatory possibility?
A) Essential possibility is mental, preparatory possibility is real
B) Essential possibility requires matter, preparatory does not
C) Essential possibility varies, preparatory does not
D) Essential possibility is only for eternal things, preparatory for originated

Key Takeaway
Essential possibility is a logical category, not a real entity; preparatory possibility is a real quality in matter—this distinction saves the proof for matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own talents or potential, do you treat them as mere logical possibilities (essential possibility) or as real qualities that require active preparation (preparatory possibility)? What is one concrete step you can take this week to move from theoretical potential to actual readiness?
?
The passage teaches that essential possibility is 'a mental consideration with no realization in external things.' In what areas of your life have you been living as if your potential alone were sufficient, without taking the preparatory steps needed for actualization? What would it cost you to keep delaying that preparation?
?
The author distinguishes between a possibility that is neutral to existence (essential) and one that ‘implies preference’ (preparatory). Where in your spiritual life do you notice a difference between simply being able to do good (the essential possibility of good deeds) and being actively prepared and inclined towards them? How can you cultivate that inner preparation?

The Mutakallimun's Refutation of the Fivefold Restriction
Refutation of the fivefold restriction using priority of parts of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutakallimun refuted the claim that priority is limited to five types by pointing to the priority of parts of time.

Core Idea
Priority among parts of time escapes the fivefold classification.

The passage begins by giving examples of different kinds of priority, then states the known fact that the priority of non-existence over existence is specifically temporal. It reports that the theologians rejected the restriction of priority to causality, nature, rank, honor, and time, and refuted it by showing that the priority of yesterday over today is not captured by any of the five, because yesterday and today are time itself, not events in time.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples of priority
The passage gives examples like head over neck, imam over follower, genus over species. Notice the variety: sensory, intellectual, natural, conventional.
2
Understand the claim about non-existence
It is known that the priority of the non-existence of an event over its existence is only by time.
3
Learn the mutakallimun's refutation
They pointed to the priority of parts of time, e.g., yesterday over today. This priority is not by causality, nature, rank, honor, nor by time in the usual sense.
Because yesterday and today are time, not events in time.
4
Reflect on the implication
This refutation shows that the fivefold classification is incomplete; there is a type of temporal priority that is not covered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلا من المحسوسة، وقد تكون عقلية بأن يكون ذلك بحكم العقل لكونه في الأمور المعقولة، وكل منهما قد يكون بحسب الطبع، وقد يكون بحسب الوضع، وذلك كتقدم الرأس على الرقبة، وتقدم الإمام على المأموم، وتقدم الجنس على النوع، وتقدم بعض مسائل العلم على البعض ومعلوم أن تقدم عدم الحادث على وجوده ليس إلا بالزمان والمتكلمون منعوا الحصر، وتمام الاستقرار. ونقضوه بتقدم بعض أجزاء الزمان على البعض، كتقدم الأمس على اليوم، فإنه كما ليس بالعلية والطبع والرتبة والشرف ليس بالزمان، لأن الأمس واليوم زمان لا أمر يقع في الزمان وما يقال في بيان الحصر المتقدم والمتأخر إن لم يجتمعا في الوجود فهو بالزمان، وإن اجتمعا فإن كان بينهما ترتيب بحسب الاعتبار فهو بالرتبة، وإلا فإن لم يحتج المتأخر إلى المتقدم فبالشرف، وإن احتاج فإن كان المتقدم أثرا في المتأخر فبالعلية، وإلا فبالطبع أو أن التقدم إما حقيقي يكون بحسب الأمر نفسه، فلا يتبدل باعتبار المعتبر، وإما اعتباري يقابله والأول إن كان بالنظر إلى الذات فبالطبع، وإن كان بالنظر إلى الوجود، فإن كان وجود المتأخر متبر وطاً بانقضاء وجود المتقدم فبالزمان، وإلا فبالعلية : والثاني : يفتقر لا محالة إلى مبدأ به الاعتبار، فإن كان كمالا في المتقدم فبالشرف وإلا فبالرتبة فلا خفاء في أنه ليس إلا وجه ضبط مع أن التقدم بالطبع قد يكون بالنظر إلى الوجود كما في الشرط، وأن التقدم بالزمان قد يكون للعدم دون الوجود، وبعد تمام الوجود فالزماني بالمعنى الذي ذكر فيها شامل للتقدم الذي بين أجزاء الزمان والذي بين الأب والابن بواسطة الزمان
Both of them can be sensory or intellectual, meaning that this [priority] can be by the judgment of reason because it is in intellectual matters. Each of them can be by nature or by convention, such as the priority of the head over the neck, the priority of the imam over the follower, the priority of the genus over the species, and the priority of some issues of knowledge over others. It is known that the priority of the non-existence of an event over its existence is only by time. The theologians (mutakallimun) denied the restriction and fully established [their view]. They refuted it by the priority of some parts of time over others, like the priority of yesterday over today, for it is just as it is not by causality, nature, rank, and honor, so also not by time, because yesterday and today are time, not something occurring in time. And what is said in explanation of the restriction of the prior and posterior: if they do not coexist in existence, it is by time; if they coexist, then if there is an order between them according to consideration, it is by rank; otherwise, if the posterior does not need the prior, it is by honor; if it does need it, then if the prior is an effect in the posterior, it is by causality; otherwise it is by nature. Or that priority is either real (haqiqi), which is according to the matter itself, so it does not change by the consideration of the considerer, or conventional (i'tibari) corresponding to it. The first, if it is with respect to essence, it is by nature; if with respect to existence, then if the existence of the posterior is cut off by the cessation of the existence of the prior, it is by time; otherwise, by causality. The second: it inevitably requires a principle by which it is considered; if it is a perfection in the prior, it is by honor; otherwise, by rank. There is no doubt that this is a way of regulation, although priority by nature may be with respect to existence as in the condition, and priority by time may be for non-existence without existence, and after the completion of existence, temporal priority in the sense mentioned includes the priority between parts of time and that between father and son by means of time.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage begins by giving examples of priority (temporal, natural, conventional) and then states the known fact that the priority of non-existence over existence is specifically temporal. It reports that the mutakallimun rejected the fivefold restriction of priority to causality, nature, rank, honor, and time, and refuted it by noting that priority among parts of time (e.g., yesterday over today) is not captured by any of these five, since parts of time are time themselves, not entities in time. The passage then presents two alternative classifications: one based on coexistence and need (if not coexistent → time; if coexistent and ordered by consideration → rank; if no need → honor; if need and prior is cause → causality; else nature), and another based on real versus conventional priority, with further subdivision by essence, existence, and perfection. The author concludes by noting that nature-priority can relate to existence (as in conditions) and temporal priority can be for non-existence, and that after full existence, temporal priority includes both parts of time and relations like father and son through time. The passage is a detailed terminological classification from kalam works.

جزء الزمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all priority can be reduced to the five types: causality, nature, rank, honor, and time.
Correction: The passage shows that the priority of parts of time (like yesterday over today) is not covered by any of these, because parts of time are time itself.

Checkpoint
What example did the mutakallimun use to refute the fivefold restriction of priority?
A) Priority of the head over the neck
B) Priority of yesterday over today
C) Priority of the imam over the follower
D) Priority of genus over species

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun refuted the restriction of priority to five types by demonstrating that the priority of parts of time (yesterday over today) does not fit any of the five categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own life, do you tend to assume that things that happen earlier are the cause of later events? How might this lesson help you reconsider that assumption, especially in matters of faith where Allah's decree transcends temporal causality?
?
The mutakallimun used a simple observation about time to overturn a complex classification. Where in your own thinking might you be clinging to an elaborate but incomplete framework, ignoring a plain truth that could dissolve it?
?
If priority of parts of time is not causal, natural, rank, or honor, then what does it mean for your understanding of time itself? Are you living as if time is just a container for events, or can you see it as a created thing that itself has order from Allah?

Alternative Classifications of Priority
Two alternative classifications of priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two alternative ways of classifying priority: one based on coexistence and need, and another based on real vs conventional priority.

Core Idea
Priority can be classified by coexistence/need or by reality/convention.

After refuting the fivefold restriction, the passage presents two systematic classifications of priority. The first divides priority based on whether the prior and posterior coexist and, if so, the relationship between them (need, causation, etc.). The second distinguishes real priority (based on the thing itself) from conventional priority (based on a consideration), further subdividing by essence, existence, and perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the first classification (coexistence-based)
Identify the decision tree: if not coexistent -> time; if coexistent -> then consider order, need, causality.
2
Understand the sub-branches
If there is considerational order -> rank; if no need -> honor; if need and prior is effect in posterior -> causality; else -> nature.
3
Read the second classification (real vs conventional)
Real priority is based on the thing itself and does not change. Conventional priority depends on a consideration.
4
Note the subdivisions of real priority
By essence -> nature; by existence -> time or causality.
5
Note the subdivisions of conventional priority
If perfection in prior -> honor; else -> rank.
Also note the concluding remarks about nature-priority and temporal priority.

A) By causality

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Consider your relationship with God. Are you prioritizing His commands as a matter of real priority (essential) or merely conventional (based on your mood)? This lesson asks you to examine the foundation of your spiritual priorities and commit to aligning them with reality.

Priority Without Time and Two Types of Temporal Priority
Sanusi presents a non-temporal priority and two types of temporal priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that there is a type of priority not requiring time, and that temporal priority can be either with a time interval or without (realization before).

Core Idea
Some priority precedes without time; temporal priority is twofold.

In previous discussions, we saw several types of priority: causal, natural, rank, honor. Now Sanusi introduces a further type that does not involve time at all—the priority of non-existence over existence. This challenges the assumption that all priority requires a temporal framework. He then presents a view that divides temporal priority itself into two kinds, one of which also does not require a time interval.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key terms for priority types.
The passage begins with 'فيكون من التقدم بغير العلية...'
2
Identify the non-temporal priority
Find the sentence that describes a priority that does not require time. What example is given?
The priority of the non-existence of an event over its existence is given.
3
Analyze the two types of temporal priority
Look for 'التقدم الزماني على وجهين'. What are the two types? How do they differ?
One involves prior in time, the other involves prior realization without time.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider: if there is a priority without time, does every event need to be preceded by time? Why does Sanusi mention this?
This shows that not every priority is temporal, and temporal priority itself can be non-temporal in one sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيكون من التقدم بغير العلية والطبع والرتبة والشرف تقدم لا يفتقر إلى زمان يقع فيه المتقدم والمتأخر، فيجوز أن يكون تقدم عدم الحادث على وجوده من هذا القبيل. فلا يثبت كون كل حادث مسبوقاً بالزمان ولا يضرنا عن الزمان تسمية مثل هذا التقدم زمانياً على ما قال بعضهم : أن التقدم الزماني على وجهين : أحدهما : أن يكون المتقدم حاصلاً في زمان قبل زمان المتأخر كما بين الأب والابن. وثانيهما: أن يكون تحقق المتقدم قبل تحقق المتأخر من غير أن يكون في زمان كما بين الأمس واليوم . وقال بعضهم : إن التقدم الزماني بالحقيقة هو الذي بين أجزاء الزمان وإنما يعرض الغير بواسطته، إذ لا معنى لتقدم الأب على الابن، إلا تقدم زمانه على زمانه ، حتى لو أريد بالتقدم الحقيقي، ما يستغني عن الواسطة لم يتناول هذا القسم، وحصر بعضهم التقدم في الذي بالعلية والذي بالطبع ذاهباً إلى أن التقدم بالرتبة والتقدم بالشرف، راجعان إلى الزمان لأن معنى تقدم مكان على آخر أن زمام الوصول إليه قبل زمان الوصول إلى الآخر، ومعنى تقدم الجنس على النوع أن زمان الأخذ، والشروع في ملاحظته قبل زمان الأخذ في النوع ، ومعنى تقدم المعلم على المتعلم أن فيه صفة توجب تقدمه في المجلس أو في الشروع في الأمور، فيعود إلى الزمان بوسط أو بلا وسط وأن التقدم الزماني راجع إلى التقدم بالطبع، لأن السابق من الأجزاء المفروضة للزمان معد لوجود اللاحق وشرط له كالحركة، فالتقدم
Thus, there is a type of priority besides causality, nature, rank, and honor that does not require a time in which the prior and posterior occur. So it is possible that the priority of the non-existence of an event over its existence is of this kind. Thus, it is not established that every event is preceded by time, nor does it harm us to call such priority 'temporal' based on what some said: 'Temporal priority is of two types: one is that the prior occurs in a time before the time of the posterior, as between father and son. The second is that the realization of the prior occurs before the realization of the posterior without being in time, as between yesterday and today.' And some said: 'Veritable temporal priority is that which is between parts of time, and it only applies to others by means of it, since there is no meaning to the priority of father over son except the priority of his time over his time. So if by real priority is meant that which is independent of a medium, it does not include this category.' And some restricted priority to that by causality and that by nature, holding that priority by rank and priority by honor are reducible to time, because the meaning of the priority of one place over another is that the time of reaching it is before the time of reaching the other, and the meaning of the priority of genus over species is that the time of taking and starting to observe it is before the time of taking in the species, and the meaning of the priority of the teacher over the student is that he has a quality that necessitates his priority in the session or in starting matters; thus it returns to time with or without a medium. And that temporal priority returns to priority by nature, because the preceding of the supposed parts of time is a preparation and condition for the existence of the subsequent, like motion. Thus priority...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on types of priority. It begins by concluding that there exists a type of priority not captured by causality, nature, rank, honor, or time—specifically the priority of non-existence over existence. This leads to the implication that not every event is preceded by time. The passage then presents two sayings: one divides temporal priority into two types (one where the prior is in a time before the posterior's time, another where realization precedes without being in time), and another saying restricts true temporal priority to relations between parts of time, considering other temporal priorities as derivative. Finally, the passage reports the view of some who restrict all priority to causality and nature, arguing that rank and honor are reducible to time (through analysis of place, genus, teacher examples), and that temporal priority itself is reducible to natural priority, since earlier parts of time are preparatory for later parts like motion. This shows a tendency to minimize the types of priority.

Key Terms
تقدم زماني
تقدم بالعلية
تقدم بالطبع
تقدم بالرتبة
تقدم بالشرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All priority necessarily involves time.
Correction: There is a type of priority (e.g., non-existence over existence) that does not require time, and even temporal priority can be defined without a time interval.

Checkpoint
What example does Sanusi give for a priority that does not require time?
A) Father over son
B) Non-existence over existence
C) Yesterday over today
D) Cause over effect

Key Takeaway
Not all priority requires time; temporal priority itself has a non-temporal form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You habitually measure your life by time—past, present, future. But if non-existence can be prior without time, what does that say about the reality of your beginning before you were born? Does that thought change how you view your current existence?
?
When you consider your sins before repentance, do you assume they are 'temporally prior' in a way that makes them distant? The passage shows priority can be timeless. How does that affect your urgency to repent now?
?
You often think of your intentions as coming before actions. But is that priority temporal or non-temporal? If your intention precedes without time, how responsible are you for actions that follow much later? Let this reflection humble you.

Reduction of Rank and Honor to Time, and Temporal to Nature
Reductionist views: rank/honor to time, temporal to natural priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments that priority by rank and honor are reducible to temporal priority, and temporal priority itself is reducible to natural priority.

Core Idea
All priority ultimately reduces to natural priority.

After discussing various types of priority, some scholars argue that rank and honor are not independent but reducible to time. They analyze examples like place, genus, and teacher-student to show that these priorities involve temporal precedence. Moreover, they argue that temporal priority itself is a form of natural priority, because earlier parts of time prepare for later parts, similar to how a cause prepares for its effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the different views reported.
The passage starts with 'وقال بعضهم : إن التقدم الزماني بالحقيقة...'
2
Identify the view on real temporal priority
What does 'some said' about true temporal priority? Only between parts of time?
They say it is only between parts of time; other cases are metaphorical.
3
Understand the reduction of rank and honor
How does the passage reduce priority of place, genus, and teacher to time? Look for the reasoning.
Through analysis of reaching time, observation time, and session precedence.
4
See the reduction of temporal to natural
Why is temporal priority considered a natural priority? What analogy is used?
Because earlier parts of time are preparatory for later parts, like motion.

فيكون من التقدم بغير العلية والطبع والرتبة والشرف تقدم لا يفتقر إلى زمان يقع فيه المتقدم والمتأخر، فيجوز أن يكون تقدم عدم الحادث على وجوده من هذا القبيل. فلا يثبت كون كل حادث مسبوقاً بالزمان ولا يضرنا عن الزمان تسمية مثل هذا التقدم زمانياً على ما قال بعضهم : أن التقدم الزماني على وجهين : أحدهما : أن يكون المتقدم حاصلاً في زمان قبل زمان المتأخر كما بين الأب والابن. وثانيهما: أن يكون تحقق المتقدم قبل تحقق المتأخر من غير أن يكون في زمان كما بين الأمس واليوم . وقال بعضهم : إن التقدم الزماني بالحقيقة هو الذي بين أجزاء الزمان وإنما يعرض الغير بواسطته، إذ لا معنى لتقدم الأب على الابن، إلا تقدم زمانه على زمانه ، حتى لو أريد بالتقدم الحقيقي، ما يستغني عن الواسطة لم يتناول هذا القسم، وحصر بعضهم التقدم في الذي بالعلية والذي بالطبع ذاهباً إلى أن التقدم بالرتبة والتقدم بالشرف، راجعان إلى الزمان لأن معنى تقدم مكان على آخر أن زمام الوصول إليه قبل زمان الوصول إلى الآخر، ومعنى تقدم الجنس على النوع أن زمان الأخذ، والشروع في ملاحظته قبل زمان الأخذ في النوع ، ومعنى تقدم المعلم على المتعلم أن فيه صفة توجب تقدمه في المجلس أو في الشروع في الأمور، فيعود إلى الزمان بوسط أو بلا وسط وأن التقدم الزماني راجع إلى التقدم بالطبع، لأن السابق من الأجزاء المفروضة للزمان معد لوجود اللاحق وشرط له كالحركة، فالتقدم
Thus, there is a type of priority besides causality, nature, rank, and honor that does not require a time in which the prior and posterior occur. So it is possible that the priority of the non-existence of an event over its existence is of this kind. Thus, it is not established that every event is preceded by time, nor does it harm us to call such priority 'temporal' based on what some said: 'Temporal priority is of two types: one is that the prior occurs in a time before the time of the posterior, as between father and son. The second is that the realization of the prior occurs before the realization of the posterior without being in time, as between yesterday and today.' And some said: 'Veritable temporal priority is that which is between parts of time, and it only applies to others by means of it, since there is no meaning to the priority of father over son except the priority of his time over his time. So if by real priority is meant that which is independent of a medium, it does not include this category.' And some restricted priority to that by causality and that by nature, holding that priority by rank and priority by honor are reducible to time, because the meaning of the priority of one place over another is that the time of reaching it is before the time of reaching the other, and the meaning of the priority of genus over species is that the time of taking and starting to observe it is before the time of taking in the species, and the meaning of the priority of the teacher over the student is that he has a quality that necessitates his priority in the session or in starting matters; thus it returns to time with or without a medium. And that temporal priority returns to priority by nature, because the preceding of the supposed parts of time is a preparation and condition for the existence of the subsequent, like motion. Thus priority...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on types of priority. It begins by concluding that there exists a type of priority not captured by causality, nature, rank, honor, or time—specifically the priority of non-existence over existence. This leads to the implication that not every event is preceded by time. The passage then presents two sayings: one divides temporal priority into two types (one where the prior is in a time before the posterior's time, another where realization precedes without being in time), and another saying restricts true temporal priority to relations between parts of time, considering other temporal priorities as derivative. Finally, the passage reports the view of some who restrict all priority to causality and nature, arguing that rank and honor are reducible to time (through analysis of place, genus, teacher examples), and that temporal priority itself is reducible to natural priority, since earlier parts of time are preparatory for later parts like motion. This shows a tendency to minimize the types of priority.

تقدم بالشرف

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rank and honor are independent types of priority not reducible to time or nature.
Correction: The passage argues they are reducible to time, and time itself is reducible to natural priority.

Checkpoint
According to the view that restricts priority to causality and nature, to what are rank and honor reducible?
A) Time
B) Causality
C) Nature
D) Both time and causality

Key Takeaway
Rank and honor reduce to time; time reduces to natural priority, making nature and causality the only fundamental types.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the priority of a teacher over student is ultimately reducible to time (via quality leading to precedence in session), does that reduce the respect you owe your teacher to mere temporal convenience? How does this affect your attitude in learning?
?
You likely prioritize certain acts of worship based on time (e.g., praying on time). This lesson suggests temporal priority is just natural priority (cause-effect). Does that mean your prayer time is merely a natural condition, not a spiritual priority? How would you explain the difference?
?
The passage reduces honor and rank to time. If someone honors you, is it just because you happened to be earlier? How does this challenge your desire for status? Will you still seek honor knowing it may be empty of real essence?

Definition and Two Types of Real Priority
Defines real priority and its two types: by causation and by nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of real priority (al-taqaddum al-ḥaqīqī) and the distinction between its two types: by causation and by nature.

Core Idea
Real priority means the posterior depends on the prior, but the prior is independent.

The author begins by defining real priority and immediately splits it into two fundamental categories. Before diving into debates, he establishes the common meaning shared by both types. This lesson lays the groundwork for understanding causal and natural priority.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage carefully once without overanalyzing. Let the author's words establish the framework.
2
Identify the common meaning
Find the sentence that states what is common between the two types. Note that the posterior needs the prior, but not vice versa.
3
Note the key difference
The text says that in priority by causation, the prior benefits the posterior's existence; in priority by nature, it does not. This is the crucial distinction.
This distinction will be used in later discussions about causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحقيقي هو الذي بالعلية أو بالطبع والمعنى المشترك بينهما كون المتأخر محتاجاً في تحققه إلى المتقدم من غير احتياج للمتقدم إليه، إلا أن المتقدم في الذي بالعلية هو المفيد لوجود المتأخر، ولا كذلك في الذي بالطبع، والمعتبر هل هو العلة التامة أم الفاعلية؟ فيه تردد، فعلى الأول يكون المتقدم والمتأخر بالعلية متلازمين وجوداً وعدماً . وعلى الثاني : قد توجد ذات المتقدم بدون ذات المتأخر بأن ينتفي بعض شروط التأثر، والمتقدم بالطبع لا يستلزم المتأخر وجوداً بل عدماً، والمتأخر يستلزمه وجوداً لا عدماً، وأما بالنظر إلى وصفي التقدم والتأخر فبين كل متقدم ومتأخر تلازم وجوداً وعدماً ، لكونهما متضايفين، لكن إذا اعتبرا من قسم واحد فإن تضايف المتقدم بالطبع مثلا، إنما هو مع المتأخر بالطبع لا بالعلية أو الزمان أو الرتبة أو الشرف، وعلى هذا قياس سائر الأقسام ، والمعنى المشترك بين التقدم بالعلية، والتقدم بالطبع، قد يقال له التقدم بالذات، وقد يقال له التقدم بالطبع، ويخص ما بالعلية باسم الذاتي، يسمى التقدم بالطبع تقدماً بالذات. بمعنى أن المتقدم مقوم محتاج إليه باعتبار الذات. والحقيقة دون مجرد الموجود كما في العلية، فإن ذات الاثنين لا تتم ولا تعقل بدون الواحد ولا خفاء في أن هذا إنما هو في الجزء دون الشرط، فالحكم ليس بكلي على ما يشعر به ظاهر عبارة المواقف.
The real (priority) is that which is by causation or by nature, and the common meaning between them is that the posterior is in need, in its realization, of the prior without the prior being in need of it. However, the prior in that which is by causation is the one that benefits the existence of the posterior, but not so in that which is by nature. And the consideration is: is it the complete cause or the efficient (cause)? There is hesitation in it. On the first (view), the prior and the posterior by causation are mutually concomitant in existence and non-existence. On the second, the essence of the prior may exist without the essence of the posterior by some conditions of being affected being absent. And the prior by nature does not necessitate the posterior in existence but (necessitates it) in non-existence, and the posterior necessitates it in existence not in non-existence. As for the consideration of the two descriptions of priority and posteriority, between every prior and posterior there is mutual concomitance in existence and non-existence, because they are correlatives. But if they are considered from one division, then the correlation of the prior by nature, for example, is only with the posterior by nature, not by causation or time or rank or honor; and on this is the analogy of the remaining divisions. And the common meaning between priority by causation and priority by nature is sometimes called priority by essence, and sometimes called priority by nature, and what is by causation is specified by the name 'essential'; priority by nature is called priority by essence, meaning that the prior is a constituent (muqawwim) needed in terms of essence. And the reality is without mere existence as in causation, for the essence of two does not subsist or be conceived without the one, and it is not hidden that this is only in the part, not the condition; thus the judgment is not universal according to what the apparent wording of al-Mawaqif suggests.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage defines real priority (al-taqaddum al-ḥaqīqī) and clarifies its two primary divisions: priority by causation (al-‘illiyya) and priority by nature (al-ṭab‘). The author states that the common meaning shared by both is that the posterior is dependent on the prior for its realization, while the prior is not dependent on the posterior. However, the key difference is that in priority by causation, the prior actively brings about the existence of the posterior (as a cause), whereas in priority by nature, this active causation is absent. The author then discusses the ambiguity regarding whether the cause considered is the complete cause (al-‘illa al-tāmma) or merely the efficient cause (al-fā‘iliyya). If the complete cause is meant, cause and effect are mutually concomitant in existence and non-existence; if only the efficient cause, the prior may exist without its effect due to missing conditions. Next, the author distinguishes priority by nature: the prior does not entail the posterior's existence (only its non-existence is impossible if the prior exists?), and the posterior entails the prior's existence. Then he explains that the descriptions of priority and posteriority are correlatives (muḍāyifān), meaning they mutually imply each other in thought, but only within the same type (e.g., priority by nature correlates with posteriority by nature, not with other types). The author then notes that the common meaning of these two types is sometimes called priority by essence (bi al-dhāt), but also applied to priority by nature specifically. Priority by causation is called essential (dhātī). Finally, the author clarifies a nuance: in causation, the prior is a constituent (muqawwim) of the posterior's essence, not a mere condition (sharṭ). This distinction is drawn from al-Mawaqif, indicating that the judgment is not universal.

Key Terms
التقدم الحقيقي
التقدم بالعلية
التقدم بالطبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority by nature and priority by causation are essentially the same.
Correction: Priority by causation involves active causation, while priority by nature does not.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes priority by causation from priority by nature?
A) In priority by causation, the prior is the efficient cause of the posterior's existence; in priority by nature, it is not.
B) Priority by causation implies temporal priority, while priority by nature does not.
C) Both are identical in meaning.
D) Priority by nature involves a condition, while priority by causation involves a part.

Key Takeaway
Real priority means the prior is independent of the posterior, and it comes in two types: causal and natural.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a relationship where you are the 'posterior'—you need the other person, but they do not need you. How does the lesson's definition of real priority (posterior needs prior, prior does not need posterior) help you accept this asymmetry without resentment? Commit to expressing gratitude to that person today.
?
Consider a responsibility you have where you are the 'prior' for someone else (e.g., parent, teacher, leader). Does your role resemble causal priority (you actively bring about their growth) or natural priority (you simply precede them without direct influence)? How does this distinction change your sense of duty? Identify one concrete action to take this week that aligns with the correct type.
?
The author hesitates whether the cause is the complete cause or the efficient cause. In your own life, when you succeed or fail, do you tend to attribute it to a single efficient cause or the complete cause? How might this hesitation refine your gratitude or accountability? Write down one area where you need to consider a more complete causal picture.
